<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16904983178989384890">Sandra Brown's two previous novels, <em>Unspeakable</em> and <em>Fat Tuesday</em>, earned her a loyal band of romantic suspense fans and <em>The Alibi</em> is sure to increase the following. Mixing a little murder, some corruption, and a good bit of illicit romance, this novel makes the golf courses of Charleston, South Carolina, seem as seedy and fascinating as the back alleys of Chinatown.<p> Hammond</p></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16904983178989384890">Sandra Brown's two previous novels, <em>Unspeakable</em> and <em>Fat Tuesday</em>, earned her a loyal band of romantic suspense fans and <em>The Alibi</em> is sure to increase the following. Mixing a little murder, some corruption, and a good bit of illicit romance, this novel makes the golf courses of Charleston, South Carolina, seem as seedy and fascinating as the back alleys of Chinatown.<p> Hammond Cross wants to be the district attorney, and for years he has proven himself to be a man of high principles and irreproachable character. When his investigations turn up evidence of the corruption of local tycoon Lute Pettijohn, Hammond has no doubt about what is the right thing to do--even when his own father is under suspicion. However, this simple debate becomes complicated when Pettijohn is murdered and Hammond's alibi is a night of forbidden passion with the suspected murderess, Dr. Alex Ladd.</p><p> Brown's quick dialogue, character quirks, and plot twists help give a modern bent to the classic detective tale. While some of the characters prance across the pages with a predictability that would make Dashiell Hammett proud (the drunk-makes-good assistant, the light-hair-dark-history socialite) most of the characters show refreshing individuality. As Hammond's internal conflict intensifies--and the passion and danger do, too--readers will find all criticisms vanishing as they blast their way through this suspenseful page-turner. <em>--Nancy R.E. O'Brien</em></p></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16904983178989384890">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1074442037">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1074442037" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/12125670-sharon" class="left imgcol" title="?Sharon?"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1417537732p2/12125670.jpg" alt="?Sharon?" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1074442037?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 11, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12125670-sharon" class="user" title="?Sharon?">?Sharon?</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/30347.The_Alibi" title="Paperback 9780446618670" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1074442037">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17105241865838717816"><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/alibicollage_zpsccc9d814.jpg.html"> <img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo alibicollage_zpsccc9d814.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418351998i/12753739.jpg" /></a><br /><br />I know I must sound like a broken record right but I truly enjoy all of the Sandra Brown books that I have read so far. Well, there was one that fell a little short for me but all the others have been such fantastic reads for me.<br /><br />The Alibi is one of my top three SB books. This one takes us to Charlotte, South Carolina where we meet the sexy Hammond Cross and the stunning Alex Ladd. <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/3e285b4b-01dc-485b-bbad-64535a4ef9fb_zpsfb092ff3.jpg.html"> <img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo 3e285b4b-01dc-485b-bbad-64535a4ef9fb_zpsfb092ff3.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418351998i/12753740.jpg" /></a><br /><br />With each book I have read, there is something a little extra that I end up loving. Whether it is the location, th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17105241865838717816"><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/alibicollage_zpsccc9d814.jpg.html">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo alibicollage_zpsccc9d814.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418351998i/12753739.jpg" /></a><br /><br />I know I must sound like a broken record right but I truly enjoy all of the Sandra Brown books that I have read so far. Well, there was one that fell a little short for me but all the others have been such fantastic reads for me.<br /><br />The Alibi is one of my top three SB books. This one takes us to Charlotte, South Carolina where we meet the sexy Hammond Cross and the stunning Alex Ladd. <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/3e285b4b-01dc-485b-bbad-64535a4ef9fb_zpsfb092ff3.jpg.html">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo 3e285b4b-01dc-485b-bbad-64535a4ef9fb_zpsfb092ff3.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418351998i/12753740.jpg" /></a><br /><br />With each book I have read, there is something a little extra that I end up loving. Whether it is the location, the side characters or even the writing style based on the date of publication, I fall in love with something different. The little “extra” I loved in this one was that things got shaking between the sheets within the first 20%. :) That is almost unheard of in SB books. And I have to say she can write some pretty sexy cabins scenes.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/469ad2e7-8574-4bac-a193-fad74fabdca4_zps1e25b79c.jpg.html">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo 469ad2e7-8574-4bac-a193-fad74fabdca4_zps1e25b79c.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418351998i/12753741.jpg" /></a><br /><br />Hammond and Alex find each other at a local fair. He was her knight in shining armor, saving her from some persistent men. A ride on Ferris wheel, a walk on the pier and a flirtatious dance has Hammond wanting more. <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/4dd38e69-0f67-4dc8-9e04-63d61a54fab1_zpsbb89d043.jpg.html">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo 4dd38e69-0f67-4dc8-9e04-63d61a54fab1_zpsbb89d043.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418351998i/12753742.jpg" /></a><br /><br />But Alex resist and leaves alone only to find herself in Hammonds arms a short time later. Hammond is feeling things that he knows he shouldn’t but he has to have her. They head to Hammond's cabin and share a night of heated passion, indulging in their desires. But when the morning comes, so does a sense of dread, when Hammond finds himself alone.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/c3a377a8-115c-47bf-a59a-bbe36e2417ce_zpsb1409567.jpg.html">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo c3a377a8-115c-47bf-a59a-bbe36e2417ce_zpsb1409567.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418351998i/12753743.jpg" /></a><br /><br />The allusive romantic connection between the two main characters created a different type of conspiracy that made the story even more captivating. The mystery and suspense in this one centers around the murder of Lute Pettijohn, who is a ruthless businessman and cheating husband. <br /><br />Many would have reasons for wanting him dead but nothing appeared to be clear cut. I had so many questions, a few theories but each time I thought I was getting somewhere, a twist was thrown in and I was back to wondering. I didn’t know who to trust, the good guys or the bad guys<br /><br />The all-around push and pull with this one was fantastic. I loved the depth in character SB gave to Hammond and Alex. Both were perfectly flawed which made them so appealing. And it never fails that she serves up a plot that has been thickened by intriguing side character. <br /><br />Rory, Steffi, Davee and Loretta all brought something different to this story. Rory was a bit of an ass. You’ll struggle with liking him or not but I think in the end you will like him just like I did. Steffi was your classic bitch with a capital B! Davee was fabulous!! Her personality was so colorful. And Loretta, she didn’t have a huge part in the story but there was just something about her.<br /><br />Without doubt this one comes highly recommended. I think I say this with every SB book review I write. Even though the romance takes a back seat to the mystery and suspense, every sexy morsel you get is truly delicious. You will love Hammond and Alex. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17105241865838717816">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1069354641">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15260410736879641724"><strong>5 STARS</strong><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430870176i/14773163._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Wow!!! It’s been a while since I’ve read a Sandra Brown book…And damn, have I missed them! And l have to say that this is a difficult book to review, as I don’t want to slip up and give anything away. <br /><br />Trust me, with this one… Just go in blind. Don’t read any reviews or even plot descriptions. Just start reading. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430870176i/14773162._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><strong>Hammond Cross</strong><br /><br />Just know that there are some incredibly juicy characters that await you. The writing is fabulous as usual, and the intrigue undeniable. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430871569i/14773317._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><strong>Alex Ladd</strong><br /><br /><strong> <em> The dense air was</em></strong></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15260410736879641724"><strong>5 STARS</strong><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430870176i/14773163._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Wow!!! It’s been a while since I’ve read a Sandra Brown book…And damn, have I missed them! And l have to say that this is a difficult book to review, as I don’t want to slip up and give anything away. <br /><br />Trust me, with this one… Just go in blind. Don’t read any reviews or even plot descriptions. Just start reading. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430870176i/14773162._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><strong>Hammond Cross</strong><br /><br />Just know that there are some incredibly juicy characters that await you. The writing is fabulous as usual, and the intrigue undeniable. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430871569i/14773317._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><strong>Alex Ladd</strong><br /><br /><strong>
  <em> The dense air was redolent with the tantalizing aromas of cooking food — junk food.</em>
</strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430871569i/14773316._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>
  <em> “Where up north are you from?<br />“Why?”<br />“Because you are obviously ill-bred and very rude.”</em>
</strong><br /><br />But this one has a little treat… yes, we get the sexy stuff right upfront! No slow build on this baby.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430871992i/14773356._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>
  <em> How to describe that burst of clarity when one knows that his life has only just now begun, that everything that’s happened before was rot compared to this, and that nothing will ever be the same again?</em>
</strong><br /><br />It takes place in Charleston, South Carolina. A town that I’ve visited many times. And there is no better place for a murder/mystery/thriller/romance if you ask me. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430870176i/14773166.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>
  <em> He had met her less than a week ago — less than a week — but he had never been more sure of anything in his life. Never before had he been so physically attracted to a woman. He had never felt such a cerebral, spiritual, and emotional connection to anyone.</em>
</strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430872216i/14773378._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />I sort of predicted the outcome quite early, but the story kept me guessing until the end. I always knew how I wanted it to end… and lets just say that… that’s all I’m going to say.<br /><br /><strong>
  <em> “Don’t be a Boy Scout.”</em>
</strong><br /><br />LOL! Loved the book. Go read it! </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer746964240">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17425488888741947458">I know I said the exact same thing about every other Sandra Brown novel I had read, but <em>The Alibi</em> truly is the best romantic-suspense ever to be written. And this time I'm sticking to my guns (well, at least until August, when her next one - <em>Mean Streak</em> - will be out).<br /><br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4005181-nell?shelf=sandra-brown" class="actionLinkLite">sandra-brown</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4005181-nell?shelf=romantic-suspense" class="actionLinkLite">romantic-suspense</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer274141523">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8664878403246988466">One of my favourite Sandra Brown novels.<br /><br />Loved the relationship between Alex and Hammond; and Hammond and Davee.<br /><br />Right from the get go Steffi comes across as harsh. I know she was trying to get ahead in a "man's world" but she seemed to hate every female.<br /><br />The mystery aspect was great. All I know is that it wasn't Alex or Hammond. Everyone one else was up for grabs.<br /><br />Wished there was an epilogue.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer45958828">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12910733754859271608">The absolute best Sandra Brown book ever. Hammond Cross is the best hero she has ever penned. The book moves at a fast pace. The ending is excellent! Ah... so tempted to give it 5 stars but only God rates a 5. I have 3 copies of the Alibi for fear something might happen to one and then I'd be without. I keep a copy on my bookshelf, my desk at work, and in my car. That way I am covered. There are very few books I am that anal about but this book along with Sharon Sala's Out of the Dark and Anne S</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12910733754859271608">The absolute best Sandra Brown book ever. Hammond Cross is the best hero she has ever penned. The book moves at a fast pace. The ending is excellent! Ah... so tempted to give it 5 stars but only God rates a 5. I have 3 copies of the Alibi for fear something might happen to one and then I'd be without. I keep a copy on my bookshelf, my desk at work, and in my car. That way I am covered. There are very few books I am that anal about but this book along with Sharon Sala's Out of the Dark and Anne Stuart's Ritual Sins I definitely covet.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_708596893">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/708596893" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3691807-julie" class="left imgcol" title="Julie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446483226p2/3691807.jpg" alt="Julie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/708596893?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 31, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3691807-julie" class="user" title="Julie">Julie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/30347.The_Alibi" title="Paperback 9780446618670" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3691807-julie?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3691807-julie?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3691807-julie?shelf=netgalley" class="actionLinkLite">netgalley</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3691807-julie?shelf=suspense" class="actionLinkLite">suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer708596893">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4762826826809655123">Oh, Sandra Brown!! This woman kills me. I just don't know what I would do without her books!!! I'm beginning to wonder if I have some sort of addiction problem. I just can't get enough of her novels. Okay. All gushing aside, lets rip this book apart and see what's going on within the pages. <br /><br />If you've read my reviews before, you know how much I love a flawed character. Sorry, but the more messed up they are, the more I love them. Come on, it's got to be easy to write the PERFECT character. Everyt</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4762826826809655123">Oh, Sandra Brown!! This woman kills me. I just don't know what I would do without her books!!! I'm beginning to wonder if I have some sort of addiction problem. I just can't get enough of her novels. Okay. All gushing aside, lets rip this book apart and see what's going on within the pages. <br /><br />If you've read my reviews before, you know how much I love a flawed character. Sorry, but the more messed up they are, the more I love them. Come on, it's got to be easy to write the PERFECT character. Everything is great in their life and basically, lead a perfect, unblemished existence. How boring must that be?!? I don't want shit to go right for me all the time. Sure, I think that it would be nice sometimes ... especially when I feel like my world is spiraling out of control because our two boys are screaming at the top of their lungs while chasing each other around the house because one of them looked out the others window or some other nonsense. At those moments, I have a bad mommy thought and it's usually that they will end up running into each other and bop heads ... knocking each other out. Hey ... I love our boys but they are a bit much sometimes. Soooo ... uh ... I have no idea where I was going with that ... oh. I love that my life isn't perfect. I want all the trials and tribulations ... that's what life is for!! I just think that a truly flawed character would be the most difficult to write and I totally respect an author that is able to do that. Hats off to Sandra Brown for writing the most perfectly flawed characters every time. <br /><br />The book itself ... I loved. I know ... shocker, right? But can you imagine wanting to get away from your life for a night and then (what you think is) fate, drops the most perfect yin to your yang, right in front of you?? I'd like to say that this happened with my husband but if I'm being perfectly honest, that man annoyed the ever loving crap out of me the first day that I met him. He wouldn't stop talking and as if it couldn't get any worse, he only wanted to talk about Ozzy Osbourne! He totally had has a man crush on Ozzy. I mean, I love my husband now ... but back then, I would have happily karate chopped his Adam's apple in an effort to get him to quiet down. Okay, okay ... I'm getting back on track. Where were we ... oh ... meeting your better half and experiencing an instantaneous and all encompassing love ... yeah ... great start to the book!! I love how all of Brown's novels start with just dropping you into the middle of the story. <br /><br />The Alibi really kept me interested the whole time that I was reading. I didn't feel a lag or boredom and I didn't find myself skimming very often ... I do happen to do that quite a bit. I'm not proud of skimming but I've got to raise two children who don't leave me much sanity or patience to work with.<br /><br />You can NEVER go wrong with a Sandra Brown book. Ever. Well ... unless you're talking about one that I haven't read yet and then you're on your own. But for the ones I've read, they're amazing. Pick it up. Now. And no, I'm not paid by Sandra Brown to say that. But I totally wouldn't turn down a few bucks if I was ... <br /><br />** <a rel="nofollow" href="http://littlemissbookmark.blogspot.com/" target="_blank">http://littlemissbookmark.blogspot.com/</a> **</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4762826826809655123">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1185842142?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 30, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4796594-pooja-jeevagan" class="user" title="Pooja Jeevagan">Pooja Jeevagan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/30347.The_Alibi" title="Paperback 9780446618670" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1185842142">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13312754170066100965">Coming from someone who rarely gives out 5 star (just 10&amp; of all read books maybe and even rarer to thrillers)...and damn, I have too many freaking reasons for it, including but not limited to:-<br /><br />- it manages to keep the suspense....even when it dedicates last 50-60 pages pointing in a person's direction you don't feel is right, it keeps the mystery...any novel that is able to keep it for 80&amp; of the span, is worth it...<br />- its a mystery book, but such soft mystery that half the book; you won</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13312754170066100965">Coming from someone who rarely gives out 5 star (just 10&amp; of all read books maybe and even rarer to thrillers)...and damn, I have too many freaking reasons for it, including but not limited to:-<br /><br />- it manages to keep the suspense....even when it dedicates last 50-60 pages pointing in a person's direction you don't feel is right, it keeps the mystery...any novel that is able to keep it for 80&amp; of the span, is worth it...<br />- its a mystery book, but such soft mystery that half the book; you won't even care for it...you would be rooting for some people on personal front<br />- it came from a woman...with all due attempts to refrain from gender bias, I don't really trust woman with mysteries (there are exceptions like Lisa Jackson now n then)<br />- it was the first book I read by the author and I have already hoarded 4 more of hers to be next in line (I know I chew out all books of authors I like and have my fingers crossed for her to become an author I would stalk for new work release)<br />- lastly, but most importantly, a mystery book which makes your eyes go misty even for 2 minutes...no matter how sentimental I might be as a person or what my mood was when I was reading that part, this gal definitely nailed it...<br /><br />Phew...I was going through the reader's block...taking ages to finish a book...delaying starting a new one...and here I find her; she made sure I complete off the mammoth of a book that I thought would take me 2 weeks to finish in least considering by low time and here I was done in less than 2 days! Gal I am definitely picking more of yours (specially the one that was first published in the year I was born....after all, I have one tricky challenge to finish this year...or maybe in two ;) )</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer231672171">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3160032825832157579"><strong>REVIEW OF AUDIOBOOK; JUNE 3, 2014<br />Narrator: Dennis Redfield.</strong><br /><br />One of the best SB's I've read. Nothing she's written in recent years can match this 1999 murder mystery.<br /><br />The MCs are flawed, vulnerable and fighting for survival - Hammond Cross, for his career, Dr Alex Ladd, for the same <em>and</em> her life. My thoughts about Hammond ran along the lines of 'not another think-with-my-dick hero', "it's black and white, dickhead!" and "you just met her, how can you be so besotted!" so in a way, Hammond Cross, cur</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3160032825832157579"><strong>REVIEW OF AUDIOBOOK; JUNE 3, 2014<br />Narrator: Dennis Redfield.</strong><br /><br />One of the best SB's I've read. Nothing she's written in recent years can match this 1999 murder mystery.<br /><br />The MCs are flawed, vulnerable and fighting for survival - Hammond Cross, for his career, Dr Alex Ladd, for the same <em>and</em> her life. My thoughts about Hammond ran along the lines of 'not another think-with-my-dick hero', "it's black and white, dickhead!" and "you just met her, how can you be so besotted!" so in a way, Hammond Cross, currently the Special Assistant Solicitor of Charleston's DA's office, is not your traditional or formulaic romance hero. He knows he's being stupid but can't fight it; he knows it's a career-ender yet he chooses that route. He's human, but he's also intrinsically good. Therein lies Hammond's dilemma and his battle against his feelings for Alex and doing what's right.<br /><br />Alex, our heroine, is the successful psychologist who battled her own way out of an abused childhood. Her encounter with Hammond at the fair where they dance gazing into each other's eyes, is reminiscent of Cinderella running away at the stroke of midnight, leaving Prince Charming to wonder who this stranger is that has captivated him. Only in this case, Prince Charming manages to make Cinderella change her mind mid-flight and end up in his cabin having sex all night long. In this case, too, Prince Charming turns out to be a knight in tarnished armor who, instead of riding to Cinderella's rescue, has to build an airtight case against her that will get her the death penalty, if he does his job.<br /><br />While Hammond Cross' character is more clear-cut and WYSIWYG, Alex, by contrast, has secrets. Big, bad secrets that come back to bite her in the worst way so that even the chance encounter between her and Hammond at the fair is not what it seems.<br /><br />The secondary characters, in particular, Davee (the victim's widow), Smilow (the lead detective), Steffi (Hammond's lover and colleague) are all well fleshed out as is Alex's half-brother, Bobby Trimble. Davee and Smilow have a history and it left me sad because I liked Davee more than any other character, even the heroine. I particularly detested Steffi even though she's very smart, highly perceptive and a great investigator. I don't know why she's a lawyer; she'd have done better as Smilow's partner than the assistant DA that she is. I detest her because I hate that the hero, flawed as he may be, would be having a sexual relationship with such an unlikeable piece of work. I still hate it even though Hammond breaks it off with her immediately upon his return from his cabin. Throughout much of the book, I couldn't help wishing Steffi would get offed next.<br /><br />This 1999 book stands up very well despite it being almost 15 years since it was written. I did not find it dated at all, unlike one reviewer here, and also recommend that if you haven't read this book, not to read the review here that contains a spoiler because the reviewer reveals who the murderer is. Most times, reviewers use the spoiler tags to comment on a significant event or detail <em>BUT NOT</em> the identity of a perp. In the case of The Alibi, I rec that you not spoil the story but sit back, enjoy the mystery and investigation, and how Hammond chooses the course that lets him be true to himself, even if it means losing his shot at the top post.<br /><br />Hammond's and Alex's romance is poignant at times and I was emotionally-invested in it despite the story being more of police procedura/suspense. I felt Alex's wistfulness as she expressed her wish to Hammond and his response. <br /><br /><em><strong>Alex:</strong> “I was thinking what it would be like to dress up and go out on a date with you. To dinner. A movie. Out in public and for all the world to see.”<br /><strong>Hammond:</strong> “Maybe. Someday.”</em><br /><br />Plain, simple words. No literary brilliance here but served its purpose. <br /><br />That also sums up my feelings about The Alibi.<br /><br />Oh yes, <strong>the Narrator</strong>. <br />Dennis Redfield did a very good job in terms of pacing and expressiveness. I could have done with more differentiation between male and female, though, so in that respect he doesn't make the list of fav male narrators. I don't like his voice either so I wish this book, in particular, I would have loved to have narrated by Slezak or Gigante, even Wopat whose only book I have is <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.audible.com/search/ref=a_search_tseft?advsearchKeywords=the+crush+sandra+brown&amp;filterby=field-keywords&amp;sprefix=the+crush">The Crush</a>.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3160032825832157579">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8869549190036686617">Wow I finally finished this book.... Took me long enough. I gave this book a 3 star rating because I did enjoy it, but I felt that the book took way too long to get to the point and didn't keep me turning the pages quite as fast.<br /><br />This story was about a prosecutor named Hammond Cross who goes to clear his head one evening and decides to visit a fair where he runs into a beautiful woman whom he just has to talk to. At the end of their little escapade, he wakes up to find her gone. Pissed off royally he heads back to Charleston, South Carolina, where he lives, and works, and finds that a very prestigious man, Lute Pettijohn has been murdered! <br /><br />What's the shocking part? He's going to be the prosecutor... Who's the main suspect? The lovely woman he was entertaining last night, Alex Ladd...... But if she was with him, wouldn't that make him her "Alibi"? <br /><br />Anyway - it was an interesting read at times, kind of boring others. All in all - Sandra Brown is a good author - but I wouldn't reread this one again!<br /><br /></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1325177795">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2175794316106887151">A quick and 'dirty' summer read involving a murder, legal culpability, and much action. An entertaining crime drama set in Charleston, SC. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1256996312">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1256996312" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/13239516-kara" class="left imgcol" title="Kara"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1348897041p2/13239516.jpg" alt="Kara" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1256996312?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/13239516-kara" class="user" title="Kara">Kara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/30347.The_Alibi" title="Paperback 9780446618670" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/13239516-kara?shelf=mystery-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1256996312">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9551303213957400267">This is a shockingly bad book about lawyers. There's some romance and a mystery involved; those were blah. The romance was based on immediate physical attraction that supposedly deepens into amazing trust and a willingness to sacrifice everything for each other . . . after one night when the two characters don't even know each others' names. I roll my eyes in disbelief.<br /><br />But the legal aspects of this story made it almost unreadable for me. Every attorney/law enforcement officer has significant con</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9551303213957400267">This is a shockingly bad book about lawyers. There's some romance and a mystery involved; those were blah. The romance was based on immediate physical attraction that supposedly deepens into amazing trust and a willingness to sacrifice everything for each other . . . after one night when the two characters don't even know each others' names. I roll my eyes in disbelief.<br /><br />But the legal aspects of this story made it almost unreadable for me. Every attorney/law enforcement officer has significant conflicts of interest--some of which we know about from the get go--and no one is voluntarily or involuntarily removed from the case. What??? Everyone is covering up for everyone else for motives that aren't clear and certainly aren't significant enough for these people to risk their livelihoods and jail time. <br /><br />Despite some popular characterizations, my experience in working with hundreds of lawyers is that they go out of their way to be honest and ethical and I simply couldn't suspend my disbelief for the sake of this story. I won't say that lawyers never make stupid or unethical decisions, but the lawyers in this book were truly, unrealistically, breaking the law or serious ethical boundaries at every turn. <br /><br />I did end up pleasantly surprised that I hadn't predict "who done it," but I had a hard time getting to that point in the story. This book isn't worth reading.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9551303213957400267">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1058631607">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1058631607" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/20083542-karen-san-diego" class="left imgcol" title="Karen San Diego"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1404021398p2/20083542.jpg" alt="Karen San Diego" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1058631607?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/20083542-karen-san-diego" class="user" title="Karen San Diego">Karen San Diego</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/30347.The_Alibi" title="Paperback 9780446618670" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/20083542-karen-san-diego?shelf=read-2014" class="actionLinkLite">read-2014</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20083542-karen-san-diego?shelf=mystery-thriller-suspense" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20083542-karen-san-diego?shelf=police-procedural" class="actionLinkLite">police-procedural</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20083542-karen-san-diego?shelf=great-twist" class="actionLinkLite">great-twist</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20083542-karen-san-diego?shelf=psycho-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">psycho-thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20083542-karen-san-diego?shelf=legal-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">legal-thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20083542-karen-san-diego?shelf=romance-drama" class="actionLinkLite">romance-drama</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20083542-karen-san-diego?shelf=romantic-suspense" class="actionLinkLite">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/20083542-karen-san-diego?shelf=5-stars" class="actionLinkLite">5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1058631607">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9343733417256254132">I wasn't expecting a romantic suspense when I put this on my to-read shelf. I mean, I am often confused by that – how do you say a novel is romantic suspense? Almost every novel has romance element in it. And after reading The Alibi, I got it – you say a book is a romantic suspense when the central idea of the book focuses on the romance and the suspense only comes second. This one qualifies.<br /><br />I am a fan of thriller novels, those which contain some romance in it because really, what good is a book</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9343733417256254132">I wasn't expecting a romantic suspense when I put this on my to-read shelf. I mean, I am often confused by that – how do you say a novel is romantic suspense? Almost every novel has romance element in it. And after reading The Alibi, I got it – you say a book is a romantic suspense when the central idea of the book focuses on the romance and the suspense only comes second. This one qualifies.<br /><br />I am a fan of thriller novels, those which contain some romance in it because really, what good is a book without love? Cheesy, huh, but can you answer that? If it is all about a crime and a cunning killer somewhere wanting to cut someone’s tongue, what good is that book? Romance is an essential part of a book, it mellows the tone and makes for the dark and gruesome parts. Most of all – it teaches you a lesson.<br /><br />Although this one’s not my forte, it is basically romance with a twist after all – I found myself liking it at some point. I became acquainted with Sandra Brown’s style, and I thought, this one’s a chick but she does her business well.<br /><br />This is my first romantic suspense, I think (or maybe not, I don’t know at all) and it had been a great start. Here is the rundown:<br /><br /><em>Born into a fine old Charleston family, Hammond Cross is determined to be the city's next district attorney - without sacrificing his integrity. <br /><br />Prosecuting the sensational murder of a real estate magnate could be his ticket into office. Yet, while Hammond anticipates his success, someone near him is plotting his downfall. Is it Steffi Mundell, colleague, ex-lover and rival? Rory Smilow, homicide detective and Hammond's avowed enemy? <br /><br />Is it the dead man's widow, wily, beautiful and Hammond's lifelong friend? Or is it Hammond's prime suspect, the mysterious woman who shares the secret that would be fatal to Hammond's ambitions?</em><br /><br />What interested me are the following:<br />1.The presence of many secondary characters, some of whom may be the villains themselves.<br />2.The dominance of female characters. Females are always very intriguing in a thriller novel.<br />3.The similarity to my recent favorite, <a title="Tell No Lies by Julie Compton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10484180.Tell_No_Lies">Tell No Lies</a> and <a title="Keep No Secrets by Julie Compton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17575415.Keep_No_Secrets">Keep No Secrets</a> by <a title="Julie Compton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/190701.Julie_Compton">Julie Compton</a>.<br />4.The trouble presented by the looming romance between the hero and a possible killer.<br /><br />These may also appeal to other readers who like a sizzling thriller with many side stories. About the plot, I have a lot of things to say. The plot is brilliant. The main hero, Hammond Cross, has a one-night-stand with a lady he doesn’t know anything about. The next day, he discovers that an important man has been murdered last night. Then, he gets the case. Then, they find a witness who can describe a lady at the scene in full detail. Then, Hammond discovers that that lady was the one he just spent a wonderful night with. And on continues the trouble.<br /><br />How do you solve a murder when you yourself don’t want to solve it? That’s the main dilemma for our hero – he doesn’t want to know because knowing the truth may lead to many complications. The prime suspect is a woman he has fallen in love with. How can he ask for her indictment? Then it turns out he also has secrets of his own. To save her, he has to admit them; he was her alibi after all. Why hasn’t he told anybody that he’d been at the scene of the crime too? <br />I liked that Sandra Brown could keep the tension up through all the switch of point of view. Most of the book’s success I think, must be attributed to her characters.<br /><br />Hammond Cross is your ordinary guy-next-door. That’s what I thought at first. He’s thirtysomething, good-looking, intelligent and has a lot going on for him. Then it turns out he has been intimate with all the concerned female characters. That was a huge turn off for me. It made him look like a slut. But of course, that twist in his character added to the spice of the story, and how he evolved towards the end.<br /><br />Alex Ladd is the mystery girl at the beginning. It turns out she is a psychologist. She’s also thirysomething, gorgeous and intelligent, and a murder suspect. As the story unfolds, we learn about her past, which makes her character a lot less credible. We learn about a guy named Bobby Trimble who shadows her every move, and we learn that she isn’t telling the whole truth to the cops and to Hammond. Who is she protecting? What is her motive? She made me think throughout.<br /><br />Steffi Mundell is the worst ever. Brash, rude and tactless, she made for the most loathed character of all. I don’t recall ever hating a character that much, even a ruthless killer (oh, I love ruthless killers). She came from a striving family but she used her brain to reach her ranks. Soon she’s working for the county solicitor’s office as assistant DA, so she and Hammond are colleagues. She is not only a good lawyer but a diligent investigator who wants a watertight case before turning to do her job, so she joins the police in the investigation. However, we learn of her envy (much of it is penis envy) towards Hammond’s success and favorable position with the bosses, her jealousy of other women, her bad attitude toward everyone, generally. She was designed to build up emotions in readers and boy, does she ever.<br /><br />Rory Smillow is the detective handling the case. He is thorough with his job, unyielding and highly respected by his inferiors and by the solicitors as well, and his actions and behavior make you think that he’s desperately trying to hide something vulnerable inside him. He isn’t very likable, and his dislike for Hammond is absolute, but he’s driven and determined.<br /><br />Davey Pettijohn is the frank, often mean, tactless but very likable widow of the Luke, the one murdered. On her first appearance, she gets in a brush-off with the eternally unlikable Steffi and makes clear she hates the lawyer. Her remarks have only two purposes: to hurt your feelings or compliment you when it is justifiable. She is the most transparent character in the book. She’s the living proof of WYSIWYG – what you see is what you get. She’s Hammond’s long-time best friend. She grew up without a father and a dysfunctional mother, but wealthy nonetheless. Then she married notorious businessman Luke Pettijohn for some reason that may interest you later, but for now, that’s about the gist of it. Everytime she’s in a scene, she steals the spotlight.<br /><br />That’s too many characters but each are as important to the final puzzle as the other. The reader will be empty-handed on the first page, but expect that each of these characters will give the answers piece by piece towards the end. Not only that; with the mystery surrounding each person comes the mystery of the murder and the dangerous affair between the two opposing figures. It has been a wonderful thrill ride with my first romantic suspense, and it’s not really a surprise that I think I may be reading more from <a title="Sandra Brown" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6218.Sandra_Brown">Sandra Brown</a>. You like this genre, I highly recommend this.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9343733417256254132">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10439958913746481957"><br />4 STARS - I REALLY LIKED IT<br />AUDIOBOOK<br /><br />This was a good one. I liked the story and I liked the characters. The male/female lead characters were great together. The only problem I had with this book, which is the same thing I've mentioned about her other thriller books, is that the endings are always too rushed. The story wraps up but only just barely. I'd really like a little more time seeing the male and female together after all the drama they suffered. If not an epilogue, at least just a bit more</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10439958913746481957"><br />4 STARS - I REALLY LIKED IT<br />AUDIOBOOK<br /><br />This was a good one. I liked the story and I liked the characters. The male/female lead characters were great together. The only problem I had with this book, which is the same thing I've mentioned about her other thriller books, is that the endings are always too rushed. The story wraps up but only just barely. I'd really like a little more time seeing the male and female together after all the drama they suffered. If not an epilogue, at least just a bit more conversation or something where we can see them happy together, even for a moment. Otherwise, this was a good read.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1241270741">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1241270741" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2794410-dee" class="left imgcol" title="Dee"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1296614853p2/2794410.jpg" alt="Dee" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1241270741?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 30, 2015</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5743864140646648557">I listened to this on audio. Usually that means I listen in the car or puttering around the house, sometimes I let it read me to sleep. In other words, when I'm not doing much and I want something to occupy my mind, I listen. I'm not one to sit in a room and listen to an audiobook. I broke that rule with this book. This one was a can't put down (or don't turn off) book for me. I enjoyed everything about it, and just when I thought I knew who the killer was, Sandra Brown threw a curve ball. I lov</span>

This one was a can't put down (or don't turn off) book for me. I enjoyed everything about it, and just when I thought I knew who the killer was, Sandra Brown threw a curve ball. I loved it, and I'm so happy I found another mystery author whose book list is long. I'm looking forward to reading many more. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7193111092116312279">Readable, but nowhere near as good as the other book I read by the author "Lethal". I'm actually surprised this is one of her more popular books. One character is more unlikable than the next and I had little to no compassion for most of them. The romantic element lacked conviction considering that it drove many of the main prognostics actions and ultimately I found it more intrusive than moving. There are too many extraneous details that are beside the point and there was absolutely no way to s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7193111092116312279">Readable, but nowhere near as good as the other book I read by the author "Lethal". I'm actually surprised this is one of her more popular books. One character is more unlikable than the next and I had little to no compassion for most of them. The romantic element lacked conviction considering that it drove many of the main prognostics actions and ultimately I found it more intrusive than moving. There are too many extraneous details that are beside the point and there was absolutely no way to solve the mystery. The author withholds too much information trying to build mystery which further hindered connection to any of the characters. There is a whole lot of misogamist attitudes embedded into the varies character's viewpoints; If I hadn't known otherwise, I would have assumed this book had been penned by a male. If this had been my first experience with the author, I wouldn't be inclined to read another of her books.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_922670453">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/922670453" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3878131-elisabeth" class="left imgcol" title="Elisabeth"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Elisabeth" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/922670453?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 09, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3878131-elisabeth" class="user" title="Elisabeth">Elisabeth</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/593756.The_Alibi" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780340836446" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3878131-elisabeth?shelf=borrowed" class="actionLinkLite">borrowed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3878131-elisabeth?shelf=2014" class="actionLinkLite">2014</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3878131-elisabeth?shelf=romantic-suspense" class="actionLinkLite">romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer922670453">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1444009292911016135">Another good and honourable man led astray by a dubious woman, although his honour is already taking a beating from his ambitious father's ties to criminal events.<br /><br />I found this very similar to Ricochet although the setting, Charleston, was much more pervasive and actually served to show how difficult it is for outsiders (Steffi Mundell) to struggle to impose themselves against those that are children of the town (Hammond, Davee). Charleston was beautifully described.<br /><br />Alex, the female lead, was int</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1444009292911016135">Another good and honourable man led astray by a dubious woman, although his honour is already taking a beating from his ambitious father's ties to criminal events.<br /><br />I found this very similar to Ricochet although the setting, Charleston, was much more pervasive and actually served to show how difficult it is for outsiders (Steffi Mundell) to struggle to impose themselves against those that are children of the town (Hammond, Davee). Charleston was beautifully described.<br /><br />Alex, the female lead, was interesting. She and an older brother were abandoned by their only parent in her early teens and her sly brother uses her blossoming sexuality to make money until they are both arrested. The brother is jailed while she, at 15, is adopted by a kindly couple and manages to turn her life around becoming a successful therapist. The sleazy brother finds her shortly before the book starts and blackmails her.<br /><br />The hero, Hammond is the hot-shot county lawyer who uncharacteristically wanders into a county fair on a saturday afternoon, meets Alex, they have a torrid night together and then she disappears the next morning without the two exchanging names.<br /><br />When he returns to Charleston he finds out that one of its premier, and most hated, citizens has been murdered. AS the case becomes a political opportunity, even before a suspect is found, information that should have beeen forthcoming by him isn't and soon he's trying to juggle too much with a detective in charge who dislikes him, an angry ex lover who is also a competitor, a childhood best friend who may have murdered her husband, a father who may have been involved in some illicit deals with the dead guy, and a mysterious woman he's obssessed with who is the main suspect in the killing.<br /><br />This takes place over only one week so its very suspenseful. A lot of fun but not the favourite of the 3 Sandra Brown's i've read. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1444009292911016135">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1198184862">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8084729496631104802">As a fan of Sandra Brown , to me this was not one of her best. Although it was a page turner I sometimes found myself bored. It was just not the one of her best. The ending for me was not the jaw drop I usually get from her books. On the other hand I did not hate it either. I would call it a good book. I personally like great books.</span>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1420202172">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1420202172" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/9398723-brooke" class="left imgcol" title="Brooke"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Brooke" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1420202172?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 28, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9398723-brooke" class="user" title="Brooke">Brooke</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/18867754-the-alibi" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/9398723-brooke?shelf=read-in-2015" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1420202172">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6214433294684341875">Sandra Brown is great at telling a story and revealing the plot bit by bit without frustrating the reader. One complaint I have about this book (and frankly several of her others) are the overly-stereotypical characters. (The Alibi had the breathtakingly beautiful maybe-innocent woman who overcomes odds to become successful, a handsome man who has had everything handed to him by his jerk of a father but who remains extremely honest and fair, the extremely ambitious woman who is a jerk to everyon</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6214433294684341875">Sandra Brown is great at telling a story and revealing the plot bit by bit without frustrating the reader. One complaint I have about this book (and frankly several of her others) are the overly-stereotypical characters. (The Alibi had the breathtakingly beautiful maybe-innocent woman who overcomes odds to become successful, a handsome man who has had everything handed to him by his jerk of a father but who remains extremely honest and fair, the extremely ambitious woman who is a jerk to everyone without any consequences, the southern rich woman who is scorned by everyone for being open with her dalliances...you get the drift.) I wish I could give her a pass on that for this one since it is one of her earlier works, but unfortunately her later novels also have this problem. I still enjoy reading her, although I can only read 1-2 at a time and then must wait a while before reading her again.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6214433294684341875">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9sT8EJms9y9TQHp512h4pD+QgIUIc/+h5OP0b3XdBueTEMPDa37j1d+YDsKpCZ4WdmdDnEGuuAuO6vH9uUjwog==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/6218.Sandra_Brown">About Sandra Brown</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/6218.Sandra_Brown"><img alt="6218" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1403026416p2/6218.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer11348778880774088800"><em>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces">See this thread for more information.</a> </em> <br /><br />Sandra Brown is the author of more than sixty New York Times bestsellers, including FRICTION (2015), MEAN STREAK (2014), DEADLINE(2013), LOW PRESSURE (2012), LETHAL (2011), &amp; TOUGH CUSTOMER (2010).<br /><br />Brown began her writing career in 1981 and since then has published over</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11348778880774088800"><em>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces">See this thread for more information.</a> </em> <br /><br />Sandra Brown is the author of more than sixty New York Times bestsellers, including FRICTION (2015), MEAN STREAK (2014), DEADLINE(2013), LOW PRESSURE (2012), LETHAL (2011), &amp; TOUGH CUSTOMER (2010).<br /><br />Brown began her writing career in 1981 and since then has published over seventy novels, bringing the number of copies of her books in print worldwide to upwards of eighty million. Her work has been translated into over thirty languages.<br /><br />In 2009 Brown detoured from romantic suspense to write, Rainwater, a much acclaimed, powerfully moving historical fiction story about honor and sacrifice during the Great Depression.<br /><br />Brown was given an honorary Doctorate of Humane Letters from Texas Christian University. She was named Thriller Master for 2008, the top award given by the International Thriller Writer’s Association. Other awards and commendations include the 2007 Texas Medal of Arts Award for Literature and the Romance Writers of America’s Lifetime Achievement Award. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11348778880774088800">...more</a>

    </div>
